- The following tables are read from: TAMS_TAR, TAMS_TAR_Sector, TAMS_WFStatus, and TAMS_Sector. No write operations are performed on these tables within this stored procedure.

Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:
- The Direction column in the TAMS_Sector table determines the order of sectors in the temporary table `#TmpAppList`. If a sector's Direction is 'BB' or 'NB', it will have an order of 1; otherwise, it will have an order of 2.
- The ColourCode column in the TAMS_TAR_Sector table is included in the temporary table `#TmpAppList`. If there is no color code for a sector, an empty string will be returned instead.
- If there are multiple applicants with the same TAR ID, they may still appear in the result set due to the grouping by TAR ID. However, this should not typically occur given the unique TARNo column in the TAMS_TAR table.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Applicant_List_Master_OnLoad
 Title: Stored Procedure Documentation - sp_TAMS_Applicant_List_Master_OnLoad

Overview:
This stored procedure retrieves a list of sectors and associated applicants based on the provided input parameters. It also performs various filtering, sorting, and grouping operations to present the data in an organized manner.

Workflow and Edge Cases:
1. The stored procedure initializes a temporary table called #TmpSector to store sector information.
2. If the temporary table #TmpAppList is commented out, the procedure will only return sector information without applicant details. Otherwise, it will join the #TmpSector and #TmpAppList tables to retrieve both sector and applicant data.
3. The procedure truncates the #TmpSector (and #TmpAppList if uncommented) before inserting new data into it.
4. It queries the TAMS_Sector table to populate the #TmpSector table with sector information based on the provided Line and TrackType, filtering for active sectors whose effective date is less than or equal to the current date and whose expiry date is greater than or equal to the current date.
5. If the temporary table #TmpAppList is uncommented, it will perform a LEFT JOIN with the #TmpSector and other tables (TAMS_TAR, TAMS_TAR_Sector, TAMS_WFStatus, TAMS_Sector) to retrieve applicant data based on various conditions.
6. The final results are returned after grouping and sorting the data in the #TmpSector table (or both #TmpSector and #TmpAppList if uncommented).

Input Parameters:
1. @Line (NVARCHAR(10)): A line identifier for the sector.
2. @TrackType (NVARCHAR(50)): The track type of the sector.
3. @ToAccessDate (NVARCHAR(20)): The access date from which to filter applicant data, formatted as YYYY-MM-DD. If NULL, no filtering will be applied on this parameter.
4. @FromAccessDate (NVARCHAR(20)): The access date up to which to filter applicant data, formatted as YYYY-MM-DD. If NULL, no filtering will be applied on this parameter.
5. @TARType (NVARCHAR(20)): A type identifier for the applicants. If NULL or empty, no filtering will be applied on this parameter.

Output Parameters:
The stored procedure does not return any output parameters directly but instead returns sector data and (optionally) associated applicant data as a result set.

Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:
1. The stored procedure reads from the TAMS_Sector, TAMS_TAR, TAMS_TAR_Sector, TAMS_WFStatus, and TAMS_Sector tables to populate the #TmpSector (and #TmpAppList if uncommented) temporary tables.
2. It writes data into the #TmpSector (and #TmpAppList if uncommented) temporary tables. These temporary tables are then used to generate the final result set.
3. The final result set may contain columns from both the #TmpSector and #TmpAppList tables (if uncommented).

Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:
1. The stored procedure uses a CASE statement to assign a Direction value of 1 or 2 based on whether the Sector's Direction is 'BB' or 'NB', respectively.
2. It filters sectors and applicants for active status (IsActive = 1) in the TAMS_Sector and WFStatus tables, respectively.
3. The procedure applies a date range filter to the sectors based on the EffectiveDate and ExpiryDate columns in the TAMS_Sector table. For applicant data, it filters based on the AccessDate column in the TAMS_TAR table.
4. If the provided Line or TrackType is not found in the TAMS_Sector table, no data will be returned for that line/track type combination.
5. If the @ToAccessDate and @FromAccessDate parameters are both NULL, the stored procedure will still filter applicant data based on the current date (GETDATE()).
6. The temporary tables #TmpSector and #TmpAppList (if uncommented) are truncated before populating with new data, ensuring no stale or previous results remain in these tables.
7. If the @TARType parameter is provided but does not match any applicant in the TAMS_TAR table, those applicants will be excluded from the final result set.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Applicant_List_OnLoad
 Title: sp_TAMS_Applicant_List_OnLoad Stored Procedure Documentation

Overview:
The `sp_TAMS_Applicant_List_OnLoad` is a stored procedure that retrieves a list of applicants, their sector, and their application status based on specific filters. It's designed to work with the TAMS (Telecommunications Network Access Management System) database.

Workflow:
1. The stored procedure first initializes two temporary tables `#TmpSector` and `#TmpAppList`.
2. It then truncates these temporary tables to ensure they are empty before populating them with data.
3. Data is inserted into the `#TmpSector` table from the `TAMS_Sector` table, filtering by the specified line, active sectors, and effective dates.
4. Data is inserted into the `#TmpAppList` table from various tables (`TAMS_TAR`, `TAMS_TAR_Sector`, `TAMS_WFStatus`, and `TAMS_Sector`), filtering by specific conditions such as active status, effective dates, line, track type, and access date range.
5. The final step is to join the data from the temporary tables based on sector ID and display the results in two orders (direction 1 and direction 2).
6. Finally, the temporary tables are dropped to free up resources.

Edge Cases:
- If the `@Line` or `@TARType` parameters are not provided, all records will be returned without filtering by these values.
- The effective dates for sectors and workflow statuses must be within the current date for the data to be considered active.
- If no data matches the specified filters, an empty result set will be returned.

Input/Output Parameters:
- `@Line` (NVARCHAR(10)): Line associated with applicants and sectors. Default is NULL.
- `@ToAccessDate` (NVARCHAR(20)): The latest access date to filter by. Default is NULL.
- `@FromAccessDate` (NVARCHAR(20)): The earliest access date to filter by. Default is NULL.
- `@TARType` (NVARCHAR(20)): Type of TAR application. Default is NULL.

Full Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:
- Reads data from the following tables: `TAMS_Sector`, `TAMS_TAR`, `TAMS_TAR_Sector`, `TAMS_WFStatus`.
- Writes data to temporary tables: `#TmpSector` and `#TmpAppList`.
- Reads the current date using GETDATE().

Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:
- The direction of the sectors is determined by whether the direction is 'BB' (Bottom-to-Top) or 'NB' (Top-to-Bottom).
- Only active sectors and workflow statuses with effective dates within the current date are considered.
- Applications with a TARStatusId of 0 are not included in the result set.
- The final result set is ordered by sector order for both directions (1 and 2).

Examples:
To retrieve applicant data for line 'ABC' and access dates between '2022-01-01' and '2022-12-31':
```sql
EXEC sp_TAMS_Applicant_List_OnLoad @Line = 'ABC', @ToAccessDate = '2022-12-31', @FromAccessDate = '2022-01-01'
```
This will return a result set containing applicants, their sectors, and application statuses for the specified line and access date range.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Approval_Add_BufferZone
 Title: Documentation for Stored Procedure [dbo].[sp_TAMS_Approval_Add_BufferZone]

Overview: This stored procedure is designed to add a buffer zone for a given TAR ID and Sector ID in the TAMS system. It checks if the specified TAR and Sector combination already exists, and if not, it inserts a new record into the TAMS_TAR_Sector table with the required details.

Workflow:
1. The stored procedure accepts three input parameters: `@TARID`, `@SectorID`, and `@Message` (output parameter).
2. It sets an internal transaction variable `@IntrnlTrans` to 0, initiates a new transaction if there are no active transactions currently, and checks if the provided TAR and Sector combination already exists in the TAMS_TAR_Sector table.
3. If the combination does not exist, it retrieves the line associated with the TAR ID from the TAMS_TAR table, then determines the sector colour code based on the type of work 'Buffer Zone'.
4. It then inserts a new record into the TAMS_TAR_Sector table with the provided TAR and Sector IDs, an 'IsBuffer' value of 1 (indicating that this is a buffer zone), the retrieved sector colour code, and an 'IsAddedBuffer' value of 1 (indicating that a new buffer zone was added).
5. If any errors occur during execution, it rolls back the transaction and sets the output message to 'ERROR INSERTING INTO TAMS_TAR'. Otherwise, it commits the transaction and sets the output message to an empty string.

Edge cases:
- If there are no active transactions, the stored procedure will begin a new one before executing any operations.
- If the provided TAR or Sector combination already exists in the TAMS_TAR_Sector table, no record will be inserted and the transaction will not be committed (or rolled back if an error occurs).
- If there is an error during execution (e.g., due to a failed insert operation), the transaction will be rolled back and the output message will be set to 'ERROR INSERTING INTO TAMS_TAR'.

Input/Output parameter descriptions:
- `@TARID` (BIGINT, IN): The unique identifier of the TAR for which a buffer zone is being added. Default value is 0.
- `@SectorID` (BIGINT, IN): The unique identifier of the Sector where the buffer zone will be added. Default value is 0.
- `@Message` (NVARCHAR(500), OUT): A message containing the result of the operation. If successful, it will be an empty string; otherwise, it will contain 'ERROR INSERTING INTO TAMS_TAR'.

Table/column interactions and read/write behavior:
- Reads from `TAMS_TAR`, `TAMS_Type_Of_Work`, `TAMS_TAR_Sector`, and `TAMS_Sector` tables.
- Writes to the `TAMS_TAR_Sector` table.

Conditional/business rules and side-effects:
- The stored procedure checks if the provided TAR and Sector combination already exists in the TAMS_TAR_Sector table. If it does, no record will be inserted, and the transaction will not be committed (or rolled back if an error occurs).
- If there is an error during execution, the transaction will be rolled back and the output message will be set to 'ERROR INSERTING INTO TAMS_TAR'.
- The stored procedure commits or rolls back the internal transaction based on whether the execution was successful or encountered errors.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Approval_Add_TVFStation
 **Stored Procedure Documentation: sp_TAMS_Approval_Add_TVFStation**

The `sp_TAMS_Approval_Add_TVFStation` is a stored procedure used to insert new records into the `[dbo].[TAMS_TAR_TVF]` table. The procedure takes three input parameters and returns an output parameter for error messages.

**Full Workflow:**
1. Initialization: The stored procedure sets an internal transaction flag and starts a new transaction if no transactions are currently active.
2. Check Existing Record: It checks if the specified combination of TARID, StationID, and TVFDirection already exists in the `[dbo].[TAMS_TAR_TVF]` table. If it does not exist, the procedure moves on to insert a new record.
3. Insert New Record: If no existing record is found, a new record is inserted into the `[dbo].[TAMS_TAR_TVF]` table with the provided TARID, StationID, and TVFDirection.
4. Error Handling: If an error occurs during the insert operation, an error message is set in the output parameter and the transaction is rolled back. Otherwise, the transaction is committed, and the procedure returns an empty error message.

**Input/Output Parameter Descriptions:**
- `@TARID` (BIGINT): The ID of the Transportation Asset Register (TAR) record. Default value is 0.
- `@StationID` (BIGINT): The ID of the TVF station. Default value is 0.
- `@Direction` (NVARCHAR(20)): The direction associated with the TVF station. It can be NULL.
- `@Message` (NVARCHAR(500)): An output parameter that holds an error message if one occurs during the execution of the stored procedure. Default value is NULL.

**Table/Column Interactions:**
- Read Behavior: The procedure reads data from the `[dbo].[TAMS_TAR_TVF]` table to check for existing records.
- Write Behavior: The procedure writes new records to the `[dbo].[TAMS_TAR_TVF]` table if no existing record is found with the provided TARID, StationID, and TVFDirection.

**Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:**
1. If no transaction is currently active, a new transaction is started.
2. The procedure checks for existing records in the `[dbo].[TAMS_TAR_TVF]` table based on TARID, StationID, and TVFDirection before attempting to insert a new record.
3. If an error occurs during the insert operation, the transaction is rolled back, and an error message is set in the output parameter.
4. If no errors occur during the execution of the stored procedure, the transaction is committed.

**Edge Cases:**
1. If the input parameters are not provided the default values (0 for TARID and StationID, NULL for Direction), and there's no existing record in the `[dbo].[TAMS_TAR_TVF]` table with the same combination of TARID, StationID, and TVFDirection, then a new record will be inserted.
2. If an error occurs during the insert operation, the stored procedure will roll back the transaction, set an error message in the output parameter, and return from the procedure.
3. If a record with the same combination of TARID, StationID, and TVFDirection already exists in the `[dbo].[TAMS_TAR_TVF]` table, then the stored procedure will not insert a new record and no side-effects will occur.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Approval_Del_BufferZone
 **Stored Procedure Documentation: dbo.sp_TAMS_Approval_Del_BufferZone**

**Purpose:** This stored procedure is designed to delete a specific record from the TAMS_TAR_Sector table based on the provided TARID and SectorID. If an error occurs during execution, it will rollback the transaction and return an error message.

**Workflow & Edge Cases:**
1. The procedure begins by initializing a local variable @IntrnlTrans to 0, indicating that no transaction is currently active.
2. It checks if there's an ongoing transaction (@@TRANCOUNT > 0). If not, it starts a new one and sets @IntrnlTrans to 1.
3. Deletes the record from TAMS_TAR_Sector where TARId equals @TARID and SectorId equals @SectorID.
4. If an error occurs during the DELETE operation, it sets the @Message output parameter with an error message and skips to the TRAP_ERROR label to rollback the transaction and return the error message.
5. If the DELETE operation is successful, it commits the transaction (if one was started) and returns the empty @Message output parameter.
6. In case of any other errors or abnormal termination, it rolls back the transaction before returning the error message.

**Input/Output Parameters:**
- @TARID: The unique identifier of the TAR record to be deleted from the TAMS_TAR_Sector table. (BIGINT = 0)
- @SectorID: The sector identifier within the TAR record to be deleted from the TAMS_TAR_Sector table. (BIGINT = 0)
- @Message: An output parameter that holds an error message if one occurs during execution. (NVARCHAR(500) = NULL OUTPUT)

**Table/Column Interactions:**
- TAMS_TAR_Sector: The table where the record deletion takes place. Columns involved are TARId and SectorId.

**Conditional/Business Rules & Side-Effects:**
1. If no transaction is ongoing, it will start one before executing the DELETE operation.
2. If an error occurs during the DELETE operation, it will rollback the transaction and return an error message.
3. It doesn't perform any additional business rules or side-effects.

**Note:** The stored procedure is intended to be used in a controlled environment where only specific TARID and SectorID combinations are valid for deletion. Ensure proper authorization and validation checks are implemented when calling this stored procedure from applications or other procedures.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Approval_Del_TVFStation
 Title: Stored Procedure Documentation - sp_TAMS_Approval_Del_TVFStation

1. **Full Workflow and Edge Cases**

The stored procedure `sp_TAMS_Approval_Del_TVFStation` is designed to delete a specific record from the `dbo.TAMS_TAR_TVF` table based on the provided TARID (Terminal Application Request ID) and TVFID (TV Factor Station ID).

- If no transaction is currently active, the stored procedure starts a new transaction and executes the DELETE statement.
- If the DELETE statement fails, an error message is set in `@Message` parameter and the transaction is rolled back. The error message is returned as the output.
- If the DELETE operation succeeds, the transaction is committed, and if there was no prior active transaction, the stored procedure returns NULL for the `@Message` parameter.
- In case of any error during the execution, the stored procedure handles it and rolls back the transaction before returning the error message.

Edge Cases:

- If either TARID or TVFID is not provided (i.e., their values are 0), the stored procedure will not execute the DELETE statement and return an error message.
- If the provided TARID does not exist in the `dbo.TAMS_TAR_TVF` table, the DELETE operation will fail, resulting in an error message.
- If there's a concurrent transaction with the same TARID and TVFID, the DELETE operation might fail due to locking issues, causing an error message to be returned.

2. **Complete Input/Output Parameter Descriptions**

| Parameter Name      | SQL Data Type | Default Value | Is Output | Description                                                                             |
|---------------------|--------------|---------------|-----------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| @TARID              | BIGINT       | 0             | No        | Terminal Application Request ID. The unique identifier for a record in the `dbo.TAMS_TAR` table. |
| @TVFID              | BIGINT       | 0             | No        | TV Factor Station ID. The unique identifier for a record in the `dbo.TAMS_TAR_TVF` table.    |
| @Message            | NVARCHAR(500) | NULL          | Yes       | An output parameter to store any error message generated during the execution of the stored procedure.  |

3. **Full Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior**

The stored procedure interacts with the `dbo.TAMS_TAR_TVF` table, reading the data to determine if it matches the provided TARID and TVFID before executing a DELETE operation. The read-write behavior is write-only when deleting records from the specified table.

4. **All Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects**

- Before executing the DELETE statement, it checks if there's an active transaction. If not, it starts a new one.
- If the provided TARID or TVFID is 0, it does not execute the DELETE statement and returns an error message.
- If the specified TARID does not exist in the `dbo.TAMS_TAR_TVF` table, the DELETE operation will fail due to a non-existent key error.
- If there's a concurrent transaction with the same TARID and TVFID, the DELETE operation might fail due to locking issues, causing an error message to be returned.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Approval_Endorse_20220930
 Title: Stored Procedure Documentation - sp_TAMS_Approval_Endorse_20220930

Overview:
The stored procedure `sp_TAMS_Approval_Endorse_20220930` is designed to handle TAR (Task, Activity, or Requisition) form approvals and endorsements within the TAMS (Training Administration Management System). It manages various workflow stages, updates related tables, sends email notifications, maintains an action log, and handles error handling.

Workflow:
1. Initialization: Checks whether there are no ongoing transactions. If not, begins a new internal transaction.
2. Message initialization: Sets the `@Message` variable to an empty string.
3. User information retrieval: Retrieves the user's ID and name based on the provided login ID.
4. TAR form approval: Updates the status of the TAR form to 'Approved', sets the action by and action on fields, and records any remarks provided.
5. TVFRunMode update (optional): If the `@TVFRunModeUpdInd` parameter is set to 1, it updates the TVF (Task, Activity, or Requisition) Run Mode for the specific TAR.
6. Next Endorser identification: Determines the ID, title, and workflow ID of the next level endorser based on the current endorser's level and workflow ID.
7. Handling edge cases: If there is no next-level endorser, the TAR form status is updated to 'Approved', an email alert is sent, and the procedure ends.
8. New Workflow row insertion (optional): If there is no existing row for the TAR and the next workflow ID in the TAMS_TAR_Workflow table, a new row is inserted with the provided parameters.
9. TAR form status update: Updates the TAR form's status to the next workflow status ID and sets the updated on and updated by fields.
10. Email notifications (optional): If the TAR type is 'Late', an email alert is sent to the next role ID.
11. Action log: Inserts a new row into the TAMS_Action_Log table with details about the approved TAR form.
12. Overriding Occupational Control Center (OCC) email notification (optional): If the workflow type is 'LateAfter', involve power is 1, and the current endorser's level is 2, it sends an email to the specified OCC role for the TAR form.
13. Error handling: In case of any errors during execution, the internal transaction is rolled back, and an error message is returned.

Parameters:
- @TARID (INTEGER): The ID of the TAR form.
- @TARWFID (INTEGER): The current workflow ID for the TAR form.
- @EID (INTEGER): The current endorser's ID.
- @ELevel (INTEGER): The current endorser's level.
- @Remarks (NVARCHAR(1000)): Remarks related to the approval or rejection of the TAR form. This is a mandatory parameter for reject and optional for approved/endorse cases.
- @TVFRunMode (NVARCHAR(50) = NULL): The new TVF Run Mode, if it needs to be updated.
- @TVFRunModeUpdInd (NVARCHAR(5) = NULL): Indicates whether the TVF Run Mode should be updated or not.
- @UserLI (NVARCHAR(50) = NULL): The user's login ID.
- @Message (NVARCHAR(500) = NULL OUTPUT): A message containing any errors that occurred during the execution of the stored procedure.

Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:
The stored procedure interacts with several tables and columns in the TAMS database, including `TAMS_User`, `TAMS_TAR`, `TAMS_TAR_Workflow`, `TAMS_Workflow`, `TAMS_Action_Log`, `TAMS_Role`, and `TAMS_User_Role`. It reads data from these tables to determine the next endorser, workflow type, role, etc., and writes data for approvals, endorsements, action logs, and email notifications.

Email Notifications:
The stored procedure sends emails related to TAR form approvals, endorsements, and OCC overrides when necessary. It uses the `sp_TAMS_Email_Apply_Late_TAR` and `sp_TAMS_Email_Late_TAR_OCC` stored procedures for sending email notifications.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Approval_Endorse_20230410
 Title: Documentation for the Stored Procedure `sp_TAMS_Approval_Endorse_20230410`

Overview:
This stored procedure is designed to handle TAR (Technical Assessment Report) approval and endorsement processes. It updates the Workflow status, assigns tasks to the next level endorser, sends emails, logs actions, and handles urgent cases if necessary.

Workflow:
1. Retrieves the current user's ID and name.
2. Updates the TAR Workflow status to 'Approved', sets ActionBy, ActionOn, and Remark fields.
3. If `TVFRunModeUpdInd` is set to 1, it updates TVF Run Mode for the specified TAR.
4. Identifies the current level endorser and retrieves relevant information like Next Endorser ID, Workflow ID, Role ID, etc.
5. If there are no more levels to endorse, sets the TAR status and sends an email if it's an urgent case.
6. Otherwise, creates a new workflow for the next level endorser and updates the TAR status.
7. Sends an email alerting the next role with the necessary information if it's an urgent case.
8. Logs the action in TAMS_Action_Log.
9. Handles special cases like UrgentAfter workflows and involves Power.
10. Commits or rolls back the transaction based on error status.

Edge Cases:
- If an error occurs during the execution of the stored procedure, it will rollback the transaction and return the error message.
- If there are no more levels to endorse, it will set the TAR status and send an email if it's an urgent case.
- If there is no next level endorser, the stored procedure will not create a new workflow for the next level endorser and move on to step 5.
- If the WorkflowType is 'UrgentAfter' and InvolvePower is set to 1, it will execute additional steps to handle OCC emails if the current level is 2.

Input Parameters:
1. @TARID (INTEGER) - TAR ID
2. @TARWFID (INTEGER) - Current Workflow ID
3. @EID (INTEGER) - Current Endorser ID
4. @ELevel (INTEGER) - Current Endorser Level
5. @Remarks (NVARCHAR(1000)) - Remarks for the approval/endorsement/rejection (mandatory for Reject, optional for Approved or Endorse)
6. @TVFRunMode (NVARCHAR(50)) - New column to be confirmed with Adeline
7. @TVFRunModeUpdInd (NVARCHAR(5)) - Indicator to Update TVF Run Mode or Not.
8. @UserLI (NVARCHAR(100)) - User Login ID
9. @Message (NVARCHAR(500) OUTPUT) - Error message if an error occurs during the execution of the stored procedure.

Output Parameters:
@Message (NVARCHAR(500) OUTPUT) - Contains any error messages that occurred during the execution of the stored procedure.

Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:
- Tables read from: TAMS_User, TAMS_TAR, TAMS_TAR_Workflow, TAMS_Endorser, TAMS_Action_Log, TAMS_Workflow
- Tables written to: TAMS_TAR_Workflow, TAMS_TAR, TAMS_Action_Log

Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:
1. If the current level endorser is the last level, it will set the TAR status and send an email if it's an urgent case.
2. If the WorkflowType is 'UrgentAfter' and InvolvePower is set to 1, it will execute additional steps to handle OCC emails if the current level is 2.
3. If there are no more levels to endorse, it will not create a new workflow for the next level endorser and move on to step 5.
4. If an error occurs during the execution of the stored procedure, it will rollback the transaction and return the error message.
5. The stored procedure sends various emails based on the approval/endorsement process and urgent cases.

 Title: Documentation for Stored Procedure `dbo.sp_TAMS_Approval_Get_Add_BufferZone`

1. **Full Workflow and Edge Cases:**
   The stored procedure `sp_TAMS_Approval_Get_Add_BufferZone` is designed to retrieve Sector ID and Sector names that have a buffer zone associated with a specific TAR ID (Transportation Asset Record). It joins the `TAMS_Sector` table with the `TAMS_TAR_Sector` table, filtering for the provided TAR ID and sectors with `IsBuffer = 1`, indicating they are buffer zones. The results are ordered by Sector ID.

   Edge cases:
   - If no sector with a buffer zone is found for the provided TAR ID, an empty result set will be returned.
   - Inconsistencies or missing data in the `TAMS_Sector` and `TAMS_TAR_Sector` tables may lead to unexpected results.

2. **Complete Input/Output Parameter Descriptions:**
   - @TARID (BIGINT): The ID of the Transportation Asset Record for which buffer zones need to be retrieved.

3. **Full Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:**
   - `TAMS_Sector` table: Read-only interaction, used to fetch sector names. Columns involved: `ID`, `Sector`.
   - `TAMS_TAR_Sector` table: Read-only interaction, used to establish the relationship between TAR ID and sectors with buffer zones. Columns involved: `TARId`, `SectorId`, `IsBuffer`.

4. **All Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:**
   - The stored procedure does not appear to have any conditional logic or business rules besides the filtering on TAR ID and IsBuffer.
   - No side effects are evident from the provided code snippet.

5. **Additional Information:**
   - This stored procedure is designed for the `dbo` schema in the context of a Transportation Asset Management System (TAMS).
   - It can be executed using the `EXEC` statement, followed by the name of the stored procedure and its input parameters enclosed within parentheses. For example:
     ```sql
     EXEC sp_TAMS_Approval_Get_Add_BufferZone 5
     ```

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Approval_Get_Add_TVFStation
 Title: Documentation for the Stored Procedure `sp_TAMS_Approval_Get_Add_TVFStation`

1. Workflow and Edge Cases
   The `sp_TAMS_Approval_Get_Add_TVFStation` stored procedure retrieves the name, direction, and ID of TVF Stations associated with a given TAR ID, as well as the TVF Run Mode for the specified TAR ID.

   Edge Cases:
   - If no TVF Station is found for the given TAR ID, an empty result set will be returned.
   - In case of any invalid or missing input parameters, an error will be thrown.

2. Input/Output Parameter Descriptions
   - @TARID (BIGINT): The unique identifier of a TAR record for which TVF Stations need to be retrieved. This is an INPUT parameter.

3. Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior
   - Reads data from the `TAMS_Station`, `TAMS_TAR_TVF` tables, and the `TAMS_TAR` table.
   - Writes no data to any tables.

4. Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects
   - A TVF Station is only considered valid if it belongs to a TAR with the provided TAR ID and has not been deleted (i.e., its `TVFDirection` column should be equal to 1).
   - The TVF Run Mode for the given TAR ID is retrieved regardless of whether there are associated TVF Stations or not.

Here's a detailed description of each query in the stored procedure:

- The first query selects and orders the name, direction, and ID of TVF Stations related to the provided TAR ID. It joins the `TAMS_Station` and `TAMS_TAR_TVF` tables on the TVF Station's ID and TVFStationId columns respectively, ensuring that only valid (active) TVF Stations are included in the result set.

- The second query selects the TVF Run Mode for the given TAR ID from the `TAMS_TAR` table based on the TAR ID provided as an input parameter.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Approval_Reject
 Title: Stored Procedure `dbo.sp_TAMS_Approval_Reject`

Overview:
This stored procedure is designed to approve or reject a TAR (Transportation Agreement Record) form within the TAMS (Transportation Asset Management System) workflow. The procedure involves updating the status and remarks of the TAR form, sending approval/rejection emails, logging actions, and handling any possible errors during execution.

Workflow and Edge Cases:
1. The stored procedure takes input parameters such as TAR ID, Current Workflow ID, Endorser ID, Endorser Level, Remarks, User Login ID, and optional Output Message.
2. If the current transaction count is zero, it begins a new internal transaction to ensure atomicity during the execution of multiple operations.
3. The procedure first retrieves various details related to the TAR form, endorsers, workflow, and user from the respective tables.
4. It updates the status of the TAR form in the `TAMS_TAR_Workflow` table to 'Rejected' with the provided Remarks and current User ID.
5. Based on the Line (NEL, DTL, or LRT), it sets the TARStatusId for the corresponding TAR record in the `TAMS_TAR` table as either 7 (Rejected) or 8 (Urgent Rejected).
6. If the TARType is 'Urgent', it sends an urgent rejection email to the relevant parties using the `sp_TAMS_Email_Urgent_TAR` stored procedure.
7. It then logs the action in the `TAMS_Action_Log` table, including details about the Line, Module, Function, TransactionID, LogMessage, CreatedOn, and CreatedBy.
8. Depending on the WorkflowType and InvolvePower of the current workflow, it may trigger additional emails to be sent (e.g., TAMS_DTL_PFR) or perform further actions.
9. If an error occurs during execution, it rolls back the internal transaction and returns an error message. Otherwise, it commits the transaction and returns the Output Message.

Input/Output Parameters:
- `@TARID` (INTEGER): The ID of the TAR form to approve or reject
- `@TARWFID` (INTEGER): The current Workflow ID associated with the TAR form
- `@EID` (INTEGER): The current Endorser ID
- `@ELevel` (INTEGER): The current Endorser Level
- `@Remarks` (NVARCHAR(1000)): Remarks to be added when rejecting a TAR form. Optional for Approval or Endorse actions.
- `@UserLI` (NVARCHAR(100)): User Login ID of the current user
- `@Message` (NVARCHAR(500) = NULL OUTPUT): A message containing any errors that occurred during execution or the success message after committing the transaction.

Full Table/Column Interactions:
- Reads data from: `TAMS_User`, `TAMS_Endorser`, `TAMS_TAR`, `TAMS_TAR_Workflow`, `TAMS_Workflow`
- Writes data to: `TAMS_TAR_Workflow`, `TAMS_TAR`, `TAMS_Action_Log`

Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:
1. If the TAR form is 'Urgent', an urgent rejection email will be sent using the `sp_TAMS_Email_Urgent_TAR` stored procedure.
2. If NEL is rejected, TARStatusId is set to 8. Else if DTL or LRT is rejected, TARStatusId is set to 7.
3. If the WorkflowType is 'UrgentAfter' and InvolvePower is 1, and the current Endorser Level is 2, it may trigger additional emails to be sent (e.g., TAMS_DTL_PFR).
4. If an error occurs during execution, it rolls back the internal transaction and returns an error message. Otherwise, it commits the transaction and returns the Output Message.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Approval_Reject_20220930
 Title: TAMS Approval and Rejection Procedure - sp_TAMS_Approval_Reject_20220930

Overview:
This stored procedure is designed to handle the approval, endorsement, or rejection of TAR forms within the TAMS system. The input parameters are used to identify the specific TAR form and the current endorser responsible for the action. The procedure performs various operations such as updating the TAR form status, sending email notifications, logging actions, and executing additional procedures based on certain conditions.

Workflow:
1. Validate the input parameters.
2. Begin a transaction if none is already ongoing.
3. Retrieve the user's information from the TAMS_User table based on the supplied login ID.
4. Update the TAR form workflow status, remark, action by, and action on fields.
5. Retrieve the current level endorser's title and other necessary information for emailing purposes.
6. Update the TAR form status based on its type (NEL, DTL, or LRT).
7. If the TAR form type is 'Late', send an email notification to the rejected TAR form.
8. Insert a log message into the TAMS_Action_Log table.
9. Based on certain conditions, execute additional procedures such as sending email notifications to OCC (Office of the Chief Compliance Officer) if required.
10. If any error occurs during execution, rollback the transaction and return an error message. Otherwise, commit the transaction and return a success message.

Edge Cases:
- If the transaction count is already ongoing, the procedure will not start a new one but instead use the existing one for all subsequent operations.
- In case of an error during execution, the transaction will be rolled back to prevent any data inconsistencies.
- The email notifications may fail due to invalid or unreachable recipient email addresses.

Input Parameters:
1. @TARID (INTEGER): TAR ID
2. @TARWFID (INTEGER): Current Workflow ID
3. @EID (INTEGER): Current Endorser ID
4. @ELevel (INTEGER): Current Endorser Level
5. @Remarks (NVARCHAR(1000)): Remarks - Mandatory for Reject, Optional for Approved or Endorse
6. @UserLI (NVARCHAR(50)): User Login ID
7. @Message (NVARCHAR(500)): Output message containing the procedure's result

Output Parameter:
1. @Message (NVARCHAR(500)): Contains a success or error message depending on the execution results.

Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:
- TAMS_TAR, TAMS_User, TAMS_Endorser, TAMS_Workflow, TAMS_Action_Log: Read and Write operations are performed on these tables as per the stored procedure's logic.
- TINYINT, INTEGER, NVARCHAR(50), NVARCHAR(1000): These data types correspond to the columns in the involved tables.

Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:
- If the line is 'NEL', the TAR form status will be updated to 8 (Rejected). Otherwise, it will be updated to 7 (Draft or Re-route).
- If the TAR form type is 'Late', an email notification will be sent to both the endorser and OCC.
- If the current level endorser's NEL Rejected = 8 Else DTL or LRT = 7, the TAR form status will be updated accordingly.
- If the WorkflowType is 'LateAfter' and InvolvePower is 1 and Current Level Endorser's [Level] is 2, an additional email notification will be sent to the OCC.

Side Effects:
- Email notifications are sent to endorsers and other parties based on certain conditions. If these emails fail due to invalid or unreachable recipient email addresses, it may result in a loss of communication with those parties.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Batch_DeActivate_UserAccount
 Title: Documentation for Stored Procedure `sp_TAMS_Batch_DeActivate_UserAccount`

1. **Procedure Name**: `MMS_DeActivate_UserAccount`
2. **Author**: jeffrey
3. **Date Created**: 26/08/2021
4. **Purpose**: This stored procedure is designed to deactivate user accounts based on a specified period defined in the TAMS_Parameters table.

### Input Parameters:
- None (The stored procedure uses a parameter from the TAMS_Parameters table.)

### Output Parameters:
- `@DeAct` (OUTPUT): This parameter is used internally to store the deactivation threshold value in months. The actual output of this stored procedure is not explicitly defined, but it affects the user accounts in the TAMS_User table.

### Table/Column Interactions and Behavior:
1. `TAMS_Parameters` (READ): Retrieves the deactivation threshold value from the `ParaValue1` column for the `ParaCode` 'DeActivateAcct'. The effective date range is also checked to ensure the value is valid at the time of execution.
2. `TAMS_User` (WRITE): Sets the `IsActive` field to 0, and updates `UpdatedBy` and `UpdatedOn` fields with the current user and timestamp respectively for all users whose account has not been active for a period greater than or equal to the deactivation threshold.

### Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:
1. The stored procedure checks if the current date is between the effective date and expiry date of the deactivation threshold value in the TAMS_Parameters table. If not, it will not update any user accounts.
2. It only considers user accounts that have been inactive for a period greater than or equal to the deactivation threshold. The deactivation is based on the `LastLogin` date in the TAMS_User table. The date is converted to a string format and then back to a datetime format using SQL Server's CONVERT function to ensure consistency across different systems.
3. The `DATEDIFF` function is used to calculate the difference between the user's last login date and the current date in months. If this difference is greater than or equal to the deactivation threshold, the user account will be deactivated (`IsActive = 0`).
4. The `UpdatedBy` field in the TAMS_User table is always set to 1 when a user account is deactivated.
5. The `UpdatedOn` field in the TAMS_User table is always set to the current date and time when a user account is deactivated.
6. The stored procedure does not check for any dependencies or cascading effects before deactivating the user accounts, which might lead to unintended consequences if there are other systems that rely on these active accounts.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Batch_HouseKeeping
 **Stored Procedure Documentation: sp_TAMS_Batch_HouseKeeping**

**1. Workflow and Edge Cases:**

The `sp_TAMS_Batch_HouseKeeping` stored procedure is designed to retrieve all records related to the TAMS (Training Administration Management System) from multiple tables. This procedure does not perform any updates or deletions on the data; it only retrieves the data for further analysis or reporting purposes.

Edge cases:
- If the parameter `DeActivateAcct` is not found or its effective date has expired, the variable @DeAct will be 0, and no records will be retrieved based on the deactivation period condition in the stored procedure.
- The query may experience performance issues if there are a large number of records in the TAMS tables or if the joins between the tables are not optimized. In such cases, indexing and query optimization techniques should be considered to improve performance.

**2. Input/Output Parameters:**
This stored procedure does not have any input parameters, and it does not return any output parameters either.

**3. Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:**

The stored procedure interacts with several TAMS-related tables:

1. **TAMS_Parameters:** Retrieves the deactivation period parameter (DeActivateAcct) for the current date.
2. **TAMS_TAR, TAMS_TAR_AccessReq, TAMS_TAR_Attachment, TAMS_TAR_Attachment_Temp, TAMS_TAR_Power_Sector, TAMS_TAR_Sector, TAMS_TAR_Station, TAMS_TAR_TVF, TAMS_TAR_Workflow:** Retrieves all records from these tables where the TARId is associated with an ID in the TAMS_TAR table.
3. **TAMS_Block_TARDate:** Retrieves all records from this table.
4. **TAMS_OCC_Auth, TAMS_OCC_Auth_Workflow, TAMS_OCC_Duty_Roster:** Retrieves all records from these tables.
5. **TAMS_Possession, TAMS_Possession_Limit, TAMS_Possession_OtherProtection, TAMS_Possession_PowerSector, TAMS_Possession_WorkingLimit:** Retrieves all records from these tables.
6. **TAMS_TOA, TAMS_TOA_Parties, TAMS_TVF_Ack_Remark, TAMS_TVF_Acknowledge:** Retrieves all records from these tables.
7. **TAMS_TAR:** Retrieves all records from this table at the end of the stored procedure.

**4. Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:**

The stored procedure does not contain any conditional business rules or side effects since it only retrieves data without making any changes to the database.

However, there is a commented update statement in the code that sets the IsActive field to 0 for users who have been inactive for a certain period (DATEDIFF(MONTH, CONVERT(DATETIME, CONVERT(NVARCHAR(10), LastLogin, 103), 103), GETDATE()) >= @DeAct). If this update statement is uncommented and executed, it would deactivate the user accounts based on the deactivation period specified in the DeActivateAcct parameter.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Batch_InActive_ResignedStaff
 Title: Stored Procedure Documentation - sp_TAMS_Batch_InActive_ResignedStaff

1. Workflow and Edge Cases
   - The stored procedure `sp_TAMS_Batch_InActive_ResignedStaff` updates, inserts, and deletes records from the `TAMS_User`, `TAMS_User_InActive` tables based on the employee resignation details present in the `VMSDBSVR.ACRS.dbo.ResignedStaff` view.
   - The procedure checks for active staff (IsActive = 1) whose LastIN date falls within the last 7 days and marks them as inactive by setting IsActive = 0 in the TAMS_User table. If the employee has resigned but is not active, their details are inserted into the `TAMS_User_InActive` table for future reference.
   - Edge cases:
      1. Employee resignation dates outside of the last 7 days are ignored.
      2. Employees without a LastIN date (empty s_lanid) are also skipped during the update, insert, and delete operations.
      3. If an employee's record already exists in the TAMS_User_InActive table, their details will not be inserted again.

2. Input/Output Parameter Descriptions
   - This stored procedure does not require any input parameters.
   - It generates output by updating, inserting, and deleting records from the mentioned tables.

3. Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior
   - Tables involved: `TAMS_User`, `TAMS_User_InActive`, `VMSDBSVR.ACRS.dbo.ResignedStaff`
   - Read behavior: The stored procedure reads the resigned staff details from the ResignedStaff view to identify the employees who have resigned within the last 7 days.
   - Write behavior: It writes updated, inserted, and deleted records in the TAMS_User and TAMS_User_InActive tables based on the identified employees.

4. Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects
   - The stored procedure checks for active staff (IsActive = 1) whose LastIN date falls within the last 7 days and marks them as inactive by setting IsActive = 0 in the TAMS_User table.
   - If an employee's record already exists in the TAMS_User_InActive table, their details will not be inserted again.
   - The stored procedure also deletes the resigned employees' records from the TAMS_User table when their details are moved to the TAMS_User_InActive table.

5. Side-Effects
   - The side-effects of this stored procedure are that it modifies data in the `TAMS_User`, `TAMS_User_InActive`, and `VMSDBSVR.ACRS.dbo.ResignedStaff` tables. It can potentially impact other processes that rely on these tables, such as user authentication, reports, etc.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Batch_Populate_Calendar
 Title: Documentation for Stored Procedure `sp_TAMS_Batch_Populate_Calendar`

Description: This stored procedure is designed to populate the `TAMS_Calendar` table with calendar data from the `TR_CALENDAR_REF` view in another database (presumably referred to as SPIN). It also includes a truncate and insert operation on a temporary table `TAMS_TR_CALENDAR_REF`.

Author: jeffrey
Date Created: August 26, 2021

Inputs/Outputs:
- @Year (NVARCHAR(4)): The year to be populated in the TAMS_Calendar table. If not provided, it is set to the current year.
- @YrFlag (INT): A flag for adding or subtracting years from the input @Year. If not provided, it is set to 0.

Workflow:
1. If the @Year and @YrFlag parameters are not provided, they are set to the current year and 0 respectively. If @YrFlag is greater than 0, @Year is incremented by that value.
2. The temporary table `TAMS_TR_CALENDAR_REF` is truncated and re-populated with data from the `TR_CALENDAR_REF` view in the SPIN database.
3. The number of calendar days for the specified year is determined, and any existing records for that year are deleted from the TAMS_Calendar table.
4. Calendar data is inserted into the TAMS_Calendar table from the temporary table `TAMS_TR_CALENDAR_REF`.
5. An attempt is made to insert calendar data into another table (presumably CALENDAR_DAY), but this part of the code has been commented out.

Edge Cases:
- If there are no existing records for the specified year in the TAMS_Calendar table, the DELETE statement will not execute, and all subsequent INSERT statements will still be performed as intended.
- If there is an error while inserting data into the CALENDAR_DAY table, an error message will be raised, and the stored procedure will terminate with an error.

Table/Column Interactions:
- TAMS_TR_CALENDAR_REF (Read/Write): A temporary table used to store calendar data before it is inserted into the TAMS_Calendar table. Columns include FR_CALENDAR_REF_DATE, FR_CALENDAR_REF_DAY, FR_CALENDAR_REF_WEEK, and FR_CALENDAR_REF_HOLIDAY.
- TAMS_Calendar (Write): The primary table being populated with calendar data. Columns include CalendarDate, CalendarDay, CalendarWeek, HolidayCode, CreatedOn, CreatedBy, UpdatedOn, and UpdatedBy.

Conditional/Business Rules:
- If the @YrFlag parameter is greater than 0, the @Year parameter is incremented by that value before any operations are performed.
- The TAMS_Calendar table is truncated and rebuilt with data from `TAMS_TR_CALENDAR_REF` every time this stored procedure is executed. If there are existing records for the specified year in the TAMS_Calendar table, they will be deleted before new records are inserted.

Side-Effects:
- This stored procedure may affect other procedures that rely on the TAMS_Calendar table, as it truncates and repopulates it with new data every time it is executed. It also attempts to insert data into another table (CALENDAR_DAY), which could have cascading effects if an error occurs during that operation.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Block_Date_Delete
 **Stored Procedure Documentation**

Title: `sp_TAMS_Block_Date_Delete`

Author: JeffreY

Created Date: January 29, 2021

Description: This stored procedure deletes a specific record from the `TAMS_Block_TARDate` table and logs the operation in the `TAMS_Block_TARDate_Audit` table.

**Full Workflow and Edge Cases**

1. The procedure accepts an integer parameter named `@BlockID`, which represents the ID of the record to be deleted from the `TAMS_Block_TARDate` table. If no `@BlockID` is provided, the stored procedure does not execute any action.
2. The procedure initializes a local variable `@IntrnlTrans` as a TINYINT with a default value of 0. This variable is used to manage transactions within the stored procedure.
3. If no active transaction exists (`@@TRANCOUNT = 0`), the procedure begins a new one.
4. The procedure then inserts the deletion record into `TAMS_Block_TARDate_Audit`, including the current date, 'D' to indicate deletion, and all columns from the selected row in `TAMS_Block_TARDate`. This is done before actually deleting the record to ensure that an audit trail of the operation is created.
5. After inserting the auditing record, the procedure then deletes the specified row (with the provided `@BlockID`) from the `TAMS_Block_TARDate` table. If there's any error during this process, the stored procedure will not continue and an error message will be returned with a code "ERROR DELETING TAMS_BLOCK_TARDATE".
6. Upon successful deletion, the stored procedure proceeds to the FORCE_EXIT_PROC label where it commits the transaction (if one is active) and returns an empty message.
7. In case of any error during the execution of the stored procedure, it will rollback the transaction and return the error message.
8. The stored procedure also includes a call to itself for testing purposes: `EXEC sp_TAMS_Block_Date_OnLoad 'NEL', ''`, `EXEC sp_TAMS_Block_Date_OnLoad 'DTL', ''`, and `EXEC sp_TAMS_Block_Date_OnLoad '', ''`. These calls are not part of the actual workflow but intended for testing purposes.

**Complete Input/Output Parameter Descriptions**

1. `@BlockID` (Input): The ID of the record to be deleted from the `TAMS_Block_TARDate` table. If not provided, no action is taken.
2. `@Message` (Output): A message indicating the status of the operation. By default, it is an empty string. If there's any error during execution, it will contain the error message "ERROR DELETING TAMS_BLOCK_TARDATE".

**Full Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior**

1. `TAMS_Block_TARDate`: This table is written to when inserting the auditing record during the deletion process, and read from to get the selected row's data for auditing purposes.
2. `TAMS_Block_TARDate_Audit`: This table is written to when inserting the auditing record during the deletion process. It records the date of the operation, its type ('D' for deletion), and all columns from the deleted row in `TAMS_Block_TARDate`.

**All Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects**

1. If no active transaction exists at the start of the stored procedure, a new one is started.
2. Before actually deleting a record from the `TAMS_Block_TARDate` table, an auditing record is created in the `TAMS_Block_TARDate_Audit` table.
3. If there's any error during the execution of the stored procedure (insertion or deletion), the transaction is rolled back and the error message is returned. Otherwise, upon successful deletion, the transaction is committed.
4. The stored procedure includes calls to itself for testing purposes which are not part of the actual workflow.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Block_Date_OnLoad
 Title: Documentation for Stored Procedure `sp_TAMS_Block_Date_OnLoad`

Overview:
The `sp_TAMS_Block_Date_OnLoad` stored procedure retrieves data from the `TAMS_Block_TARDate` table based on provided filter parameters. The results are ordered by the `BlockDate` in descending order.

Workflow and Edge Cases:
1. The stored procedure receives input parameters `@Line`, `@TrackType`, and `@BlockDate`. It checks if each parameter is NULL or an empty string. If any of these conditions are met, it considers the filter as not set, and includes all relevant rows in the result set.
2. The query selects data from the `TAMS_Block_TARDate` table, including the `ID`, `Line`, `TrackType`, `BlockDate`, `BlockReason`, and `IsActive`. The `BlockDate` is converted to a format compatible with SQL's date comparison for efficient filtering.
3. The data is sorted by the `BlockDate` in descending order.
4. If no rows match the provided filters, an empty result set will be returned.

Input Parameters:
- `@Line` (NVARCHAR(20)): The line associated with the block date record. An empty string or NULL allows all lines to be included in the result set.
- `@TrackType` (NVARCHAR(50)): The track type associated with the block date record. An empty string or NULL allows all track types to be included in the result set.
- `@BlockDate` (NVARCHAR(20)): The block date in 'yyyy-mm-dd' format. An empty string or NULL allows all block dates to be included in the result set.

Output Parameters: None (This stored procedure does not have any output parameters.)

Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:
- TAMS_Block_TARDate: The table from which data is read. Columns selected include `ID`, `Line`, `TrackType`, `BlockDate`, `BlockReason`, and `IsActive`.

Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:
There are no conditional business rules or side-effects defined in this stored procedure.

Example Usage:
```sql
EXEC sp_TAMS_Block_Date_OnLoad 'NEL', '2021-03-16', NULL;
```
The above example retrieves all block date records for line 'NEL' on March 16, 2021 (if such records exist), and sorts them in descending order by `BlockDate`. If the `@Line` or `@TrackType` parameters are not set, the query will return records that match any line or track type.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Block_Date_Save
 **Stored Procedure Documentation:**

Title: `sp_TAMS_Block_Date_Save`

Author: Reno Adipura

Creation Date: 10/03/2021

Last Modified: 10/10/2025

Description: This stored procedure is designed to save a block date for a specific line and track type in the `TAMS_Block_TARDate` table. The block date can only be saved if it meets certain conditions, such as being at least 5 weeks prior to the current date or being a future date.

**Workflow and Edge Cases:**

1. The procedure begins by declaring internal transaction control variables and initializing them to default values.
2. If there is no ongoing transaction, it starts a new one.
3. It then validates the block date based on the current date:
   - If the block date is within 5 weeks from the current date and in the same year, the validation passes.
   - If the block date is not within 5 weeks from the current date but in the same year, an error message is set.
   - If the block date is in a different year:
      - If the block date is more than 5 weeks from the current date in the same year (by considering 52 weeks as a year), the validation passes.
      - If the block date is less than 5 weeks from the current date or in the future, an error message is set.
4. The procedure checks if a block date with the given line, track type, and date already exists. If it does, an error message is set.
5. If no errors have occurred, the block date is inserted into the `TAMS_Block_TARDate` table along with other relevant data. A new identity value is captured for the inserted record.
6. The newly inserted record is also inserted into the `TAMS_Block_TARDate_Audit` table.
7. If any errors occur during execution, the transaction is rolled back and an error message is set. Otherwise, the transaction is committed, and the stored procedure ends by returning the error message (if one exists) or an empty string if everything went well.

**Input/Output Parameters:**

- `@Line` (AS NVARCHAR(20)) - The line for which the block date is being saved. This parameter is input only.
- `@TrackType` (AS NVARCHAR(50)) - The track type for which the block date is being saved. This parameter is input only.
- `@BlockDate` (AS NVARCHAR(20)) - The block date to be saved. This parameter is input only.
- `@BlockReason` (AS NVARCHAR(100)) - The reason for blocking the date. This parameter is input only.
- `@UserLI` (AS NVARCHAR(50)) - The user login ID. This parameter is input only.
- `@Message` (AS NVARCHAR(500) = NULL OUTPUT) - The error message if any occur during execution. This parameter is output only.

**Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:**

- **Read**: The procedure reads data from the `TAMS_User` table to get the user ID based on the provided login ID.
- **Write**: The procedure writes data into the `TAMS_Block_TARDate` and `TAMS_Block_TARDate_Audit` tables.

**Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:**

- The block date must be at least 5 weeks prior to the current date or in the future. If not, an error message is set.
- A block date cannot already exist with the given line, track type, and date. If it does, an error message is set.

**Side-effects:**

- The stored procedure may cause a transaction to be started and committed or rolled back based on its execution outcome.
- It inserts records into the `TAMS_Block_TARDate` and `TAMS_Block_TARDate_Audit` tables.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_CancelTarByTarID
 **Documentation for the stored procedure sp_TAMS_CancelTarByTarID**

**Overview:**
The `sp_TAMS_CancelTarByTarID` is a stored procedure designed to cancel a Tar record with the specified ID and log the action in the TAMS_Action_Log table. The cancellation process follows the workflow defined by the TARWFStatus table, checking for the appropriate status to cancel the Tar.

**Workflow:**
1. Receives input parameters `@TarId` (the Tar ID to be cancelled) and `@UID` (the User ID of the person cancelling the Tar).
2. Begins a transaction.
3. Retrieves the line for the specified TarID from TAMS_TAR table.
4. Retrieves the WFStatusId for the cancel status related to the Tar's Line and WFType ('TARWFStatus') from the TAMS_WFStatus table.
5. Retrieves the name of the user cancelling the Tar from the TAMS_User table using the provided UID.
6. Updates the TARStatusId of the specified Tar in the TAMS_TAR table.
7. Inserts a record into TAMS_Action_Log, logging the action and providing relevant details such as Line, type (TAR), activity (Enquiry-Cancel), Tar ID, reason for cancellation, current date and time, user name, and user ID.
8. If any error occurs during execution, the transaction will be rolled back.

**Edge cases:**
1. If the provided TarID does not exist in the TAMS_TAR table, the stored procedure will throw an error as no line is returned for the specified TarID.
2. If the specified WFType ('TARWFStatus') or WFStatus ('Cancel') do not have a corresponding Line and WFStatusId in the TAMS_WFStatus table, the stored procedure will throw an error as no appropriate status to cancel the Tar is found.
3. If any other error occurs during execution, the transaction will be rolled back, and the stored procedure will terminate with an error.

**Input/Output Parameter Descriptions:**
- `@TarId` (input): The ID of the Tar to be cancelled. This parameter is set to 0 by default.
- `@UID` (input): The User ID of the person cancelling the Tar. This parameter is set to 0 by default.

**Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:**
- **Read behavior:** The stored procedure reads data from TAMS_TAR, TAMS_WFStatus, and TAMS_User tables for the specified TarID, WFType, WFStatus, and User ID.
- **Write behavior:** The stored procedure writes data into the TAMS_Action_Log table to log the cancellation action and relevant details. Additionally, it updates the TARStatusId of the specified Tar in the TAMS_TAR table.

**Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:**
1. A transaction is started before any modifications are made to the database to ensure data consistency in case of an error during execution.
2. If the cancellation status for the provided Line and WFType does not exist in the TAMS_WFStatus table, the stored procedure will throw an error and roll back the transaction.
3. The TARStatusId of the specified Tar is updated only if a valid cancellation status exists and no error occurs during execution.
4. A record is inserted into TAMS_Action_Log only if the transaction successfully completes (i.e., no error occurs during execution).
5. If any other error occurs during execution, the transaction will be rolled back, and the stored procedure will terminate with an error.

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Check_UserExist
 **Stored Procedure Documentation**

Title: `sp_TAMS_Check_UserExist`
Author: Johnson
Created on: March 5, 2021
Last Modified: Not Applicable (This is a new stored procedure)

**Overview:**
The `sp_TAMS_Check_UserExist` stored procedure checks if a user exists in the TAMS_User table based on either SAPNo or LoginID provided as input parameters.

**Workflow and Edge Cases:**
1. The procedure takes two input parameters: `@SapNo` (NVARCHAR(100)) and `@LoginID` (NVARCHAR(200)). Both are optional, meaning the user can either provide one or both values.
   - If neither parameter is provided, no check will be performed, and the procedure will simply return an empty result set.
   - If only one parameter is provided (either `@SapNo` or `@LoginID`), the procedure will perform a search based on that specific input value.
   - If both parameters are provided, the procedure will perform a search based on both values (i.e., it will check for a user with the specified SAPNo and LoginID).

2. The procedure checks if the provided input parameters exist in the TAMS_User table.
   - If a matching record is found, the procedure returns a result set containing '1'.
   - If no matching record is found, the procedure does not return any result sets.

**Input/Output Parameter Descriptions:**
- `@SapNo` (NVARCHAR(100)): The SAP No of the user to check for existence in the TAMS_User table. This parameter is optional.
- `@LoginID` (NVARCHAR(200)): The Login ID of the user to check for existence in the TAMS_User table. This parameter is optional.

**Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:**
- **TAMS_User**: The only table interacted with by this stored procedure, used for checking the existence of users based on the provided input parameters.
  - `LoginID`: The Login ID column of the TAMS_User table. Used to find users if the `@LoginID` parameter is provided.
  - `SAPNo`: The SAP No column of the TAMS_User table. Used to find users if the `@SapNo` parameter is provided.

**Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:**
- If both `@LoginID` and `@SapNo` are provided, the stored procedure performs a more specific check (looking for a user with a matching SAP No and Login ID). This could potentially lead to a reduction in false positives compared to when only one parameter is provided.
- If neither `@LoginID` nor `@SapNo` is provided, no side effects or checks are performed. The procedure simply returns an empty result set.

4. The transaction is then committed if successful or rolled back in case of errors.

Edge cases:

- If the `TAMS_User_QueryDept` table does not exist or the provided user ID is invalid, the stored procedure will throw an error and rollback the transaction.

2. Deleting User Query Departments may have side effects such as breaking any queries or reports that rely on them, so it's essential to ensure data integrity before running this procedure.
3. This stored procedure uses a transaction for data consistency in case of errors. If an error occurs during the execution, the entire transaction will be rolled back, ensuring no unintended changes are made to the database.

2. The stored procedure starts by beginning a transaction.
3. It checks if there is any row in the `TAMS_User_Role` table that matches the provided user ID. If such rows exist, it proceeds to delete them. Otherwise, no operation is performed (Edge Case: No Roles for User).
4. If the user has a role with ID 1 (administrator), the procedure does not allow deletion as this role is presumably reserved and cannot be removed from users (Edge Case: Administrator Role).
5. The transaction is committed if no errors occur during execution, otherwise it is rolled back.

- If an error occurs during execution, the transaction is rolled back to maintain data integrity.

- Deletes rows from the `TAMS_User_Role` table where the `UserID` matches the provided input and the `RoleID` is not equal to 1 (administrator role).

Procedure: dbo.sp_TAMS_Depot_Applicant_List_Child_OnLoad
 Title: Stored Procedure `sp_TAMS_Depot_Applicant_List_Child_OnLoad`

Description: This stored procedure retrieves a list of applicants based on the provided parameters such as Line, TrackType, AccessDate range, TARType, and SectorID. It also filters the results based on active sectors and the current date.

Workflow and Edge Cases:
1. The stored procedure first sets the current date and creates a temporary table `#TmpAppList` to store the applicant list.
2. If the `@Line`, `@TrackType`, or `@SectorID` parameters are not provided, they default to NULL.
3. If no sectors match the provided Line and are active, an empty result set is returned.
4. If no applicants match the filter criteria within the specified date range and for the active sectors, an empty result set is returned.
5. The temporary table `#TmpAppList` is dropped at the end of the procedure.

Input/Output Parameter Descriptions:
- @Line (AS NVARCHAR(10) = NULL): The line associated with the applicant list.
- @TrackType (AS NVARCHAR(50) = NULL): The track type associated with the applicant list.
- @ToAccessDate (AS NVARCHAR(20) = NULL): The end date for the AccessDate range filter.
- @FromAccessDate (AS NVARCHAR(20) = NULL): The start date for the AccessDate range filter.
- @TARType (AS NVARCHAR(20) = NULL): The TAR type associated with the applicant list. If omitted, all TAR types are included.
- @SectorID (AS INT): The ID of the sector to filter the results by.

Full Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:
- Writes data to temporary table `#TmpAppList`.
- Reads from tables `TAMS_TAR`, `TAMS_TAR_Sector`, `TAMS_WFStatus`, and `TAMS_Sector`.

Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:
- The procedure filters the applicant list based on active sectors (`s.IsActive = 1`) and the current date (`@CurrDate BETWEEN s.EffectiveDate AND s.ExpiryDate`).
- The `TAMS_TARStatusId` field in `TAMS_TAR` is compared to the `WFStatusId` in `TAMS_WFStatus`. If it's not 0, it means the applicant status is active and included in the result set.
- The `ColorCode` column from `TAMS_TAR_Sector` is populated in the `#TmpAppList` table if available; otherwise, an empty string is used.

Example Usage:
```sql
EXEC sp_TAMS_Depot_Applicant_List_Child_OnLoad 'DTL', '01/01/2021', '30/06/2021', 'CSAPEX57', 1
```
This example retrieves the applicant list for Line `DTL`, from January 1, 2021 to June 30, 2021, and sector ID 1 using TrackType 'CSAPEX57'.

 **Stored Procedure Documentation**

Title: `sp_TAMS_Depot_Applicant_List_Master_OnLoad`

**Workflow and Edge Cases:**

This stored procedure is designed to retrieve a list of applicants for a specific depot line and sector type. The edge cases are as follows:

1. If the input parameters `@Line`, `@TrackType`, or both are null or missing, the stored procedure will return an empty result set.
2. If the specified line or track type does not exist in the TAMS_Sector table, the stored procedure will return an empty result set.
3. The effective date and expiry date of the sector in TAMS_Sector must be greater than or equal to the current date for the results to be returned.
4. If the `@ToAccessDate` and/or `@FromAccessDate` parameters are outside the access date range of any applicant, the stored procedure will return an empty result set.
5. If the TARType parameter is specified and there is no match with the applicants' TARType, the stored procedure will return an empty result set.
6. If both `@ToAccessDate` and `@FromAccessDate` are null or missing, all records will be returned regardless of access date.
7. The stored procedure creates a temporary table #TmpSector for storing sector information and a temporary table #TmpAppList (although commented out), which is not currently utilized in the final query result.
8. The final query groups and orders the results by sector order.

**Input/Output Parameter Descriptions:**

1. `@Line` - (AS NVARCHAR(10) = NULL) - Depot line number to filter applicant list for. Can be null or missing.
2. `@TrackType` - (AS NVARCHAR(50) = NULL) - Specific track type to filter applicant list for. Can be null or missing.
3. `@ToAccessDate` - (AS NVARCHAR(20) = NULL) - Access date range end point to filter applicant list for. Can be null or missing.
4. `@FromAccessDate` - (AS NVARCHAR(20) = NULL) - Access date range start point to filter applicant list for. Can be null or missing.
5. `@TARType` - (AS NVARCHAR(20) = NULL) - Applicant TAR type to filter applicant list for. Can be null or missing, but if specified it must match the TARType of the applicants in the result set.

**Full Table/Column Interactions and Read/Write Behavior:**

The stored procedure reads from and writes to the following tables:

1. `TAMS_Sector` - To retrieve sector information based on the input parameters `@Line` and `@TrackType`.
2. Temporary table `#TmpSector` - Created for storing sector information during the execution of the stored procedure.
3. (Commented out) temporary table `#TmpAppList` - Not currently utilized in the final query result, but its structure indicates it was intended to store applicant information based on the filtering conditions.

**Conditional/Business Rules and Side-Effects:**

1. The stored procedure checks if the specified sector is active (IsActive = 1) in TAMS_Sector.
2. The effective date and expiry date of the sector must be greater than or equal to the current date for the results to be returned.
3. The access date of each applicant must fall within the specified date range (`@ToAccessDate` and `@FromAccessDate`) for the applicant to be included in the final result set.
4. If both `@ToAccessDate` and `@FromAccessDate` are null or missing, all records will be returned regardless of access date.
5. The stored procedure creates a temporary table #TmpSector during its execution and drops it after the query is complete.
6. (Commented out) The stored procedure also initially created a temporary table #TmpAppList but it's not utilized in the final query result, so this part of the code doesn't currently have any effect on the output.

Overview: This stored procedure is designed to save access details for TAR (Technical Asset Report) forms in the `TAMS_TAR` table. It handles the validation, insertion, and management of transactions related to the TAR form submission for Depot TAR.

Workflow:
1. The procedure accepts input parameters that represent user-provided data for the TAR form. These parameters include details about the line, track type, access date, time slot, type, company, designation, name, office number, mobile number, email, access time from, access time to, access location, neutral gap status, exclusive status, description of work, access remark, involvement in power, power status, 13A socket status, crossover, protection type, and the user ID.
2. The procedure begins a new internal transaction if none is currently active.
3. It retrieves the user's ID from the `TAMS_User` table using the provided login ID.
4. The procedure then inserts the TAR form data into the `TAMS_TAR` table, generating a new TAR ID (`@TARID`) as an output parameter.
5. If there is an error during the insertion process, the stored procedure sets the `@Message` output parameter to reflect the error and rolls back the transaction if one is active. Otherwise, it commits the transaction and returns the success message in the `@Message` output parameter.

Edge Cases:
- If there is no active internal transaction at the beginning of the stored procedure, a new transaction will be started. However, if an error occurs during the execution of the stored procedure, the entire transaction will be rolled back, and all changes made within that transaction will be discarded.
- The `TAMS_TAR` table may have primary key or foreign key constraints that can prevent the insertion of duplicate records. In such cases, the stored procedure will return an error message in the `@Message` output parameter, and the transaction will be rolled back if one is active.

Input/Output Parameters:
- `@Line` (NVARCHAR(10)): Line number associated with the TAR form (optional).

- `@AccessTimeTo` (NVARCHAR(50)): Access time to (format: HH:mm).

- `@ProtectionType` (NVARCHAR(50)): Type of protection used during the access (optional).
- `@TARID` (BIGINT): Output parameter representing the generated TAR ID for the submitted form.
- `@Message` (NVARCHAR(500)): Output parameter containing any error messages or success messages related to the stored procedure execution.

Procedure: dbo.SP_TAMS_Depot_GetDTCAuth
 **Documentation for the Stored Procedure SP_TAMS_Depot_GetDTCAuth**

**1. Workflow and Edge Cases:**

The stored procedure SP_TAMS_Depot_GetDTCAuth retrieves Depot Authorisation records along with their associated data for a specific access date. It performs a LEFT JOIN on multiple tables to combine the data required, handling null values from the left-side tables when there is no matching record.
